This theorem is the dynamic analogue of the approximation templates of Appendix D, but integrated into a route/diagram architecture.

G.3 Pending Coherence

Pending coherence is the exact class that prevents silent publication of unresolved dynamic equivalences. Let be a proposed coherence cell whose proof obligations are not closed. Then

\alpha:P\Rightarrow Q\ \text{pending}

Thus a pending cell must carry:

an obligation set;

dependency closure;

blocking status;

a publication gate flag.

The governing law is:

Law G.7 (No Publication with Pending Coherence). Any seed, route, compiler output, or witness bundle whose dependency closure contains a pending coherence cell is not publishable in mode. It must remain blocked, residualized, or explicitly downgraded.

This law is architecturally crucial because it prevents convergence claims from outrunning their own proof obligations.

The convergence architecture must also define its target artifact families. A lawful convergence pipeline may emit:

seed artifacts in canonical normal form;

certificate skeletons for exact or -closure;

replay specifications and replay transcripts;

coherence certificates;

regression artifacts;

obligation ledgers;

publication gate checklists.

This list is exact because convergence in this manuscript is never merely mathematical. It is also executable, replayable, and governable. A convergence architecture that cannot emit these artifact families is incomplete.

The next essential structure is the compilation pipeline for convergence-bearing systems. Let be a typed program, route specification, or operator declaration. Then the deterministic convergence pipeline is:

parse and scope-validate all declarations;

type-check all routes and operators under the pinned corridor;

normalize all terms and paths to the declared normal-form regime;

compile constraints and coherence obligations into the internal IR;

emit seed artifacts and canonical hashes;

instantiate certificate skeletons;

emit replay specifications and transcript schemas;

emit diagram/coherence obligations;

emit obligation ledger and publication gate checklist.

This pipeline is not specific to one compiler dialect. It is the canonical convergence architecture of the manuscript. Any executable system that claims to participate in the manuscript’s convergent runtime must admit a lawful projection to this nine-stage body.

The architecture is governed by deterministic output law.

Law G.8 (Deterministic Output Law). For fixed program text, fixed pinned versions, fixed environment pins, and fixed dependency hashes, convergence architecture outputs must be identical up to canonical serialization.

This law is indispensable. If convergence outputs depend on accidental runtime variance, then no replay certificate can ground an -class claim. Determinism is therefore not optimization. It is the admissibility condition for convergence architecture.

The architecture must also define promotion gates. A convergence object is ready for promotion when:

all exact or -coherence obligations are closed;

all replay-integrity certificates pass;

all pending cells are absent from the dependency closure;

regression suites pass or certified migrations close the deltas;

required ledger entries are complete;

required witness and replay pointers are present.

These six conditions define the manuscript’s promotion gate. The gate is not optional. It is the exact boundary between dynamic process and canonicalized outcome.

The central convergence object of the appendix is now the Convergence Capsule:

\mathsf{Cap}_{\mathrm{conv}}=

\big(

\mathsf{SeedRef},

\mathsf{Mode},

\mathsf{Corr},

\mathsf{CellSet},

\mathsf{LedgerRef},

\mathsf{ReplayRef},

\mathsf{CertRef}

\big).

The architecture now requires exact state transitions. A convergence object may inhabit one of the following states:

\mathrm{Declared},\ \mathrm{Checking},\ \mathrm{ExactLocked},\ \mathrm{EpsLocked},\ \mathrm{Pending},\ \mathrm{Residualized},\ \mathrm{Blocked},\ \mathrm{Published},\ \mathrm{Migrated}.

requires typed route and corridor validity;

requires exact coherence closure;

requires certified -coherence;

occurs when open obligations remain but no contradiction has appeared;

occurs when unresolved obligations are ledgered and bounded for later repair;

occurs when critical dependencies fail;

or requires passage of the promotion gate;

requires a certified migration plan and replay closure.

This state system prevents the manuscript from using the word “converged” ambiguously. A process may be in a checking regime, a locked regime, or a publishable regime, and these are not the same.

The architecture must further define the relation between convergence and residualization. A residual is not an embarrassment and not a silent failure. It is a typed unresolved remainder:

\mathsf{Res}:=(\mathrm{ResID},\mathrm{Scope},\mathrm{Bound},\mathrm{Source},\mathrm{UpgradePath},\mathrm{Digest}).

the remaining gap is explicitly bounded or classifiable;

the unresolved sources are identified;

the target scope is preserved;

an upgrade path exists;

the residual is attached to the ledger.

This is the law by which the manuscript handles honest incompleteness. Residualization is the canonical Flower–Cloud bridge: motion has approached but not yet fully locked, and the remaining gap is preserved as a typed artifact rather than hidden in prose.

The major theorem of Appendix G is the Convergence Architecture Theorem.

Theorem G.9 (Convergence Architecture Theorem). Let be a declared convergence object with typed carrier, typed update family, corridor specification, witness family, replay family, and certificate family. Suppose:

the update family is lawful under the Flower operator discipline;

the relevant boundedness and approximation hypotheses of Appendix D are satisfied;

all coherence cells are either exact, -certified, or explicitly pending;

every non-exact or pending component is attached to a residual ledger;

replay is deterministic under the declared pins.

Then admits one and only one of the following lawful statuses:

exact locked,

-locked,

pending,

residualized,

blocked.

Moreover, promotion to publishable status is lawful if and only if the promotion gate closes.

Proof sketch. The hypotheses ensure that all dynamic motion is lawful, all approximation claims are certified, all unresolved obligations are explicit, and replay is stable. Therefore the process cannot hover in an undefined semantic middle state: it either closes exactly, closes within declared tolerance, remains open with explicit obligations, is residualized with explicit upgrade path, or is blocked by contradiction or missing critical dependency. Promotion beyond these states requires closure of the publication gate by definition.

This theorem is architecturally load-bearing. It says the convergence layer is semantically total. No convergence object is allowed to inhabit an unnamed limbo state.

The appendix must now specify failure modes.

A normalization drift failure occurs when paths are compared under mismatched normalizers. An untracked -failure occurs when approximate equality is asserted without a certified ledger. A pending laundering failure occurs when an open coherence cell is treated as if it were resolved. A replay divergence failure occurs when the same pinned convergence capsule yields non-identical outputs on replay. A certificate gap failure occurs when a convergence mode is asserted but the corresponding certificate family is absent. A promotion gate breach occurs when publication proceeds despite unresolved obligations, missing replay, or failed regression. Each failure corresponds to a precise architectural break and therefore to a typed issue code in implementation-level realization.

The local zero-point of Appendix G is the convergence kernel:

Z_G(\mathsf{Conv})=

\big(

\mathsf{TargetType},

\mathsf{Mode},

\mathsf{CorrDigest},

\mathsf{CellDigest},

\mathsf{LedgerDigest},

\mathsf{Truth}

\big).

Integration with surrounding appendices is exact. Appendix D provides the proof skeletons whose hypotheses and constants are concretized here. Appendix E provides the operator families and snap semantics that many convergence architectures consume. Appendix F provides translation and transport equivalences so that convergence may be compared across representations. Appendix H will bind the constants and thresholds used by these architectures. Appendix I and later appendices will make convergence transportable across embeddings, implementations, and replay protocols. Thus Appendix G stands as the compression hub of the Water row: it is the appendix where seed, proof, flow, and translation are assembled into lawful closure.

The compression principle of Appendix G is decisive. Convergence is not a mood, not a visual impression, and not an informal “close enough.” It is a typed architecture composed of state, update, corridor, coherence cells, residual ledgers, replay handles, and certificates. Only when those parts are present and lawful may the manuscript say that something has converged. Appendix G is therefore the appendix that protects the manuscript from false closure. It is the exact body by which lawful approach becomes lawful arrival.

Appendix G

Appendix H — Constant Catalogue, Threshold Regimes, and the Manifestation Ledger

Appendix H fixes the constant body of the manuscript. It is the appendix in which the variable architectures of the preceding appendices are bound to exact numerical, logical, and admissibility thresholds, and in which those thresholds are coupled to the ledger discipline that determines whether a state may lawfully seat, persist, upgrade, or be pruned. If Appendix G defines convergence architecture, Appendix H defines the constants by which convergence is judged. If Appendix D supplies proof templates for stability and approximation, Appendix H supplies the corridor constants, coherence floors, parity checks, seating thresholds, and promotion guards that turn those templates into executable law. Appendix H is therefore both catalogue and ledger: catalogue because it enumerates the constant families on which the system depends, ledger because it determines which manifested nodes satisfy those constants well enough to enter the enduring record of the manuscript.

The appendix has a dual role that must be distinguished precisely. First, it is the constant catalogue, the exact registry of corridor constants, threshold tables, comparison budgets, and audit intervals. Second, it is the manifestation ledger specification, the architecture by which objects that satisfy those thresholds are seated in persistent form. These are not separate bodies. The manifestation ledger is meaningful only relative to exact constants, and the constants are operationally relevant only insofar as they determine ledger seating, continuity, and pruning. Appendix H binds them into one law-bearing structure.

Let a manifested node be any typed manuscript object

\eta=\big(\mathrm{id},\mathrm{type},\mathrm{payload},\mathrm{witness},\mathrm{replay},\mathrm{truth},\mathrm{digest}\big)

To answer this, Appendix H defines the manifestation ledger

\mathcal{L}_H=(V_H,E_H,\Theta_H,\mathcal{A}_H,\mathcal{P}_H,\mathcal{Q}_H),

is the seated node set;

is the typed lineage and merge edge set between seated nodes;

is the constant catalogue governing admissibility;

is the audit system;

is the pruning and persistence law;

is the quarantine interface for inadmissible or degraded states.

This object is the first exact persistent memory body of the appendix field. It is not a notebook. It is not a log of everything that ever happened. It is the lawful record of what has manifested stably enough to deserve seated status.

The constant catalogue is the heart of the appendix. It is organized into five principal families.

\Theta_H=

\Theta_{\mathrm{coh}}

\cup

\Theta_{\mathrm{par}}

\cup

\Theta_{\mathrm{seat}}

\cup

\Theta_{\mathrm{prom}}

\cup

\Theta_{\mathrm{audit}}.

Here:

is the coherence constant family;

is the parity and consistency constant family;

is the seating threshold family;

is the promotion and truth-upgrade guard family;

is the audit and resynchronization interval family.

These families are irreducible. A ledger without coherence constants cannot judge crystallization. A ledger without parity constants cannot detect divergence. A ledger without seating thresholds cannot decide inclusion. A ledger without promotion guards cannot control truth escalation. A ledger without audit constants cannot preserve global identity across cycles.

The first family is the coherence constant family. Let denote the measured coherence of node . This may be instantiated differently in different chapters, but its architectural role is stable: it quantifies the degree to which the node is internally stable, witness-supported, replay-compatible, and corridor-consistent. Appendix H requires that every manifestable node be equipped with a coherence functional

\mathcal{C}: \mathcal{N}_{\mathrm{cand}} \to \mathbb{R}_{\ge 0},

\Gamma_N > 0,

\mathcal{C}(\eta)\ge \Gamma_N.

This gives the first principal theorem of Appendix H.

Theorem H.1 (Manifestation Eligibility Theorem). Let be a candidate node assigned to regime . Then is eligible for ledger seating only if

\mathcal{C}(\eta)\ge \Gamma_N

Proof. By definition of the manifestation ledger, seated nodes are precisely those that satisfy the constant catalogue . The coherence floor is an element of that catalogue. Therefore violation of the inequality excludes seating. Presence of witness and replay pins is likewise part of the seating law, so omission of those pins likewise excludes seating. The conjunction is necessary.

The second family is the parity and consistency constant family. A manifestation ledger is a temporal object. It evolves. Therefore local coherence alone is not sufficient. The ledger must also preserve global identity across recursive cycles, merges, and distributed replay contexts. To enforce this, Appendix H defines a global parity hash

\mathcal{H}_G=\mathsf{Hash}\big(\mathrm{Canon}(V_H,E_H,\Theta_H)\big),

4^4 = 256

The parity law is therefore:

Law H.2 (Global Parity Law). At every audit cadence , the manifestation ledger computes the global parity hash . If a replaying or distributed agent diverges from the canonical , the system must either exhibit a lawful migration proof that explains the drift or roll back to the last certified state. Silent parity divergence is forbidden.

This law makes the ledger more than a local notebook. It makes it the temporal anchor of the manuscript runtime.

The third family is the seating threshold family. Coherence alone is necessary but not sufficient for seating. The node must also satisfy:

witness completeness: all mandatory witness classes for the node type must be present;

replay availability: deterministic replay handle must exist if the node claims -grade truth;

address validity: canonical address must parse and normalize;

dependency closure: all parent obligations must already be seated or explicitly residualized;

truth admissibility: nodes with unresolved contradiction, quarantine flags, or failed replay may not seat in canonical form.

Thus the seating predicate is

\mathsf{Seat}_H(\eta)=

\big[

\mathcal{C}(\eta)\ge \Gamma_N

\big]

\wedge

\mathsf{Wit}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{Rep}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{Addr}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{Dep}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{Truth}(\eta).

This yields the Seating Predicate Theorem.

Theorem H.3 (Seating Predicate Theorem). A candidate node is lawfully seatable in the manifestation ledger if and only if .

Proof. The forward direction follows by definition of lawful seating. The reverse direction follows because the conjunction includes every required structural, witness, replay, address, dependency, and truth condition named by the ledger architecture. There is no additional hidden criterion. Therefore satisfaction of the conjunction is sufficient.

The fourth family is the promotion guard family. The manuscript distinguishes truth classes , and Appendix H is one of the appendices that forbids silent upward motion between these classes. A node that is merely seated is not necessarily promotable. Promotion requires additional constants and guards. Let

\Pi_H(\eta)

closure of all open residual ledgers;

exact or certified -coherence under the declared corridor;

deterministic replay success under pinned environment;

absence of unresolved conflict edges;

promotion certificate emission.

Thus:

\Pi_H(\eta)=

\mathsf{Seat}_H(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{ResClosed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{ReplayOK}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{NoConflict}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{PromCert}(\eta).

The no-silent-promotion law then becomes an exact theorem.

Theorem H.4 (No Silent Promotion Theorem). If is false, then may not be promoted to -grade canonical status, regardless of narrative plausibility or partial success.

Proof. The predicate is the exact promotion guard. Promotion without satisfying it would violate the constant catalogue and therefore the definition of lawful manifestation. Hence it is prohibited.

The fifth family is the audit family. In addition to the global parity cadence, Appendix H defines local audit constants for:

witness freshness windows;

replay expiry windows;

merge-check intervals;

pruning intervals;

ledger compaction checkpoints.

These constants are not universal scalars but typed members of . A lawful ledger implementation must declare them explicitly. The lower-dimensional crystal body may choose the canonical baseline

T_A=4^4

The manifestation ledger must also define its edge structure. A seated node does not live alone. The edge set contains typed lineage and coherence relations:

E_H\subseteq

\{\mathrm{REF},\mathrm{GEN},\mathrm{INST},\mathrm{PROOF},\mathrm{MERGE},\mathrm{RESIDUAL},\mathrm{MIGRATE},\mathrm{CONFLICT}\}.

A edge records lawful synthesis of multiple seated nodes into a new seated node. A edge records deferred incompleteness that remains attached to the node. A edge records lawful version or policy evolution while preserving lineage. A edge records hard contradiction or replay failure and blocks canonical seating or promotion until resolved. This means the ledger is not just a set of nodes but a dynamic crystal graph with persistent memory of how nodes arrived, split, recombined, or failed.

The ledger must also support pruning. Pruning is often misunderstood as deletion. In Appendix H it has a narrower and stricter meaning. The permanent truth-bearing core of a seated node is never discarded. What may be pruned are:

failed candidate metadata after quarantine;

superseded -state scaffolds once exact closure has been seated;

redundant replay intermediates once a stable proof-carrying certificate has been emitted;

nonauthoritative branch artifacts whose lineage remains preserved elsewhere.

Pruning is therefore governed by:

Law H.5 (Historical Pruning Law). No pruning operation may remove the minimal data required to reconstruct seated truth, lineage, residual history, or quarantine provenance. Pruning removes excess metadata, not truth-bearing structure.

This law ensures that the ledger remains efficient without becoming forgetful in a law-breaking way.

The quarantine interface is essential. Appendix H is not the quarantine appendix—that role belongs elsewhere—but it must define how the manifestation ledger interacts with quarantined states. If a candidate node fails seating or later loses admissibility under audit, one of three things happens:

it remains unseated and is routed to quarantine;

it is a seated node whose metadata is downgraded while truth-bearing core remains and conflict edges are emitted;

it is rolled back to a prior seated version if a lawful predecessor exists.

This gives the Quarantine Routing Law.

Law H.6 (Manifestation–Quarantine Routing Law). Any candidate or seated node whose coherence falls below threshold, whose replay diverges, whose parity fails without lawful migration proof, or whose conflict obligations remain unresolved beyond its admissible window must emit a quarantine route or rollback route. It may not remain silently seated as if valid.

The ledger also needs a merge discipline because the corpus repeatedly describes sub-ledgers merging into a main ledger. Let be lawful sub-ledgers. A lawful merge is a map

\mathsf{Merge}_H(\mathcal{L}_1,\mathcal{L}_2)\to \mathcal{L}_3

all seated nodes preserve canonical addresses or declare address migrations;

duplicate nodes are collapsed by digest and lineage equivalence;

conflicts are emitted explicitly as edges;

the resulting global parity hash is recomputed;

the merge transcript is replayable.

This yields the Ledger Merge Theorem.

Theorem H.7 (Ledger Merge Theorem). If and are lawful manifestation sub-ledgers satisfying shared corridor pins and replay discipline, then their merge is lawful if and only if duplicate collapse, conflict emission, lineage preservation, and parity recomputation are all performed.

Proof sketch. Failure of duplicate collapse produces ambiguity; failure of conflict emission hides contradiction; failure of lineage preservation destroys provenance; failure of parity recomputation leaves the merged object unauditable. Each is therefore necessary. Together they suffice to preserve the ledger laws under union.

The exact implementation boundary of Appendix H must now be stated. A manifestation ledger object must be implementable as:

class ManifestationNode(TypedDict):

    node_id: str

    node_type: str

    payload_digest: str

    witness_refs: list[str]

    replay_ref: str | None

    truth: str

    coherence: float

    regime: str

    address: str

and

class ManifestationLedger(TypedDict):

    nodes: list[ManifestationNode]

    edges: list[dict]

    constants: dict[str, float | int | str]

    parity_hash: str

    audit_tick: int

    quarantine_refs: list[str]

together with validator output:

class LedgerValidation(TypedDict):

    ok: bool

    seatable: list[str]

    blocked: list[str]

    quarantined: list[str]

    issues: list[str]

This code rigor is not optional. It is the precise expression of the appendix’s architectural claim that manifestation is a ledgered runtime discipline rather than a literary metaphor.

The relation between Appendix H and Appendix I must also be clarified. Appendix H contains the constant catalogue and manifestation seating law. Appendix I will refine one major subfamily of those constants into explicit entropy threshold tables. The distinction is therefore: Appendix H defines the ledger architecture and the generic constant families; Appendix I elaborates the thermodynamic and entropy-specific benchmark tables used by the Cloud lens. Appendix H is the catalogue and ledger body; Appendix I is one specialized threshold atlas inside that body.

A local zero-point law is required. For a seated node , define

Z_H(\eta)=

\big(

\mathrm{type},\,

\mathrm{regime},\,

\mathrm{coherence\ class},\,

\mathrm{truth},\,

\mathrm{digest}

\big).

Z_H(\mathcal{L}_H)=

\big(

\mathcal{H}_G,\,

\Theta_H,\,

\mathsf{SeatPredicateDigest},\,

\mathsf{AuditDigest}

\big).

The integration of Appendix H with surrounding appendices is exact. Appendix D provides the proof templates whose constants and tolerances are catalogued here. Appendix G provides the convergence architecture whose outcomes are seated or residualized by the current appendix. Appendix I elaborates entropy-specific threshold tables. Appendix K later consumes quarantine outputs that are routed here. Appendix L later validates and replays the seated ledger states. Appendix P later maintains and migrates them. Thus Appendix H is the hinge between proof, convergence, truth, and persistence.

The compression principle of Appendix H is that manifestation is never merely appearance. To say that something has manifested within this manuscript is to say that it has satisfied exact constant families, entered the ledger under a lawful seating predicate, survived parity and replay discipline, and either carried no residual or carried a residual openly. Appendix H therefore transforms “manifestation” from a vague word into a technical event. It is the appendix in which the manuscript learns how to remember lawfully.

Appendix H

Appendix I — Error Calculus, Entropy Threshold Tables, and Ledgered Admissibility

Appendix I defines the global error calculus of the manuscript and the ledger system that makes every approximation, truncation, threshold choice, branch ambiguity, conditioning warning, entropy excursion, and budget decision explicit, typed, serializable, replay-verifiable, and therefore governable. Its role is exact. If Appendix H establishes the constant catalogue and manifestation ledger at the level of coherence floors, seating predicates, promotion guards, and audit cadences, Appendix I refines that discipline into a full Cloud-lens calculus of uncertainty, loss, conditioning, stability, and entropy budgets. In the live corpus this role is stated directly: Appendix I is the appendix of global error envelopes, propagation rules, invariants against silent loss, geometric conditioning diagnostics, probabilistic bounds, drift detection, budget tradeoffs, and the mechanized ledger engines used by publication gates.

The appendix has three inseparable tasks. First, it defines a typed universe of error and entropy envelopes capable of expressing deterministic, interval, geometric, and probabilistic uncertainty without collapsing them into one informal “margin of error.” Second, it defines propagation laws by which such envelopes move through operator graphs, route compilers, convergence capsules, tunnel bodies, and manifestation ledgers. Third, it defines threshold tables and admissibility rules under which a node, route, compiler output, or witness bundle is classified as exact, -bounded, metastable, residual, ambiguous, or failed. Appendix I is therefore not merely a statistics appendix and not merely a tolerance appendix. It is the honesty appendix. It is the place where the manuscript formalizes what is known, what is only bounded, what is not yet closed, what is unstable, and what must be blocked from promotion.

Let denote the set of all kernel objects eligible for approximation, transport, or replay. For every , Appendix I defines an error state

\mathsf{Err}(x)=\big(\mathsf{Env}(x),\mathsf{Cond}(x),\mathsf{Bud}(x),\mathsf{Entropy}(x),\mathsf{Ledger}(x)\big),

is the envelope family assigned to ;

is the conditioning profile of the map or representation used to compute or transport ;

is the budget family within which is allowed to vary;

is the measured or bounded uncertainty load borne by ;

is the typed residual and propagation record attached to .

This decomposition is minimal. An error description without an envelope is not a bound. An error description without conditioning does not explain sensitivity. An error description without budgets does not explain admissibility. An error description without entropy does not tell whether the object is thermally or statistically stable. An error description without a ledger is not replayable and therefore cannot be trusted in canonical use.

The foundational object of the appendix is the ErrorEnvelope. The live corpus already supplies its exact schema:

\mathsf{Env}=(\mathsf{EnvID},\ \mathsf{MetricID},\ \mathsf{Form},\ \mathsf{Value},\ \mathsf{Scope},\ \mathsf{Mode},\ \mathsf{Assumptions},\ \mathsf{Deps},\ \mathsf{Tags}),

The envelope forms are finite and typed. The canonical family is:

Scalar envelope, encoding a single deterministic upper or lower error bound;

Interval envelope, encoding a closed bound ;

Vector interval envelope, encoding coordinatewise or componentwise interval bounds;

Ellipsoidal envelope, encoding a center and quadratic form for anisotropic uncertainty;

Upper-bound-only envelope, used when only one-sided safety is certified;

Lower-bound-only envelope, used when impossibility or minimum dissipation is the primary invariant;

Probabilistic envelope, encoding statements of the form

   \mathbb P(d(\widetilde x,x)\le \varepsilon)\ge 1-\delta.

These forms are not interchangeable. A scalar deterministic envelope may not silently replace a probabilistic one; an interval envelope may not be treated as ellipsoidal without a certified embedding; and an ellipsoidal envelope may not be collapsed to a scalar radius unless the collapse law and induced loss are ledgered. This gives the first exact law of the appendix.

Law I.1 (Typed Envelope Law). Every error or entropy statement must declare its envelope form explicitly. No manuscript object may change envelope class without either a proof of equivalence or an explicit residual ledger recording the induced loss.

This law is indispensable because different envelope classes support different propagation algebras. The manuscript cannot lawfully reason with them as if they were all one generic “tolerance.”

The second foundational object is the metric family. Every envelope is meaningless without a metric, norm, divergence, or pseudometric in which it is stated. Appendix I therefore adopts a typed metric identifier

\mathsf{MetricID}\in\mathcal{M}_I,

discrete Hamming-like carrier metrics;

-norms on declared function spaces;

spectral-energy seminorms;

operator norms;

enclosure metrics for interval and box regimes;

divergence measures for probabilistic or distributional comparisons;

route- or graph-distance metrics for metro objects;

entropy-like scalars where the comparison target is uncertainty load rather than direct geometric separation.

No envelope may omit its . If an argument depends on changing metric, that change is a typed transport and must be certified.

The third foundational object is the proof mode. The corpus already distinguishes proof modes and requires their explicit inclusion in the envelope schema. Appendix I fixes the canonical proof-mode ladder:

: exact symbolic or combinatorial proof;

: exact reduction to certified lower-level witnesses;

: interval or enclosure proof under declared arithmetic and conditioning;

: probabilistic or empirical proof under pinned assumptions and replayable estimator traces.

The proof mode is not an ornament. It determines what promotion is lawful. A envelope may support -grade operational trust, but it may not silently promote to exact closure unless a separate exact or enclosure proof closes the gap. This yields the next governing law.

Law I.2 (Mode-Bounded Promotion Law). An ErrorEnvelope may contribute to -grade exact publication only if its proof mode and envelope form are sufficient for the target truth class under the declared corridor. Probabilistic or empirical envelopes do not silently promote to exact closure.

This law is one of the central honesty laws of the manuscript. It prevents soft evidence from masquerading as exact law.

The appendix now defines its global propagation problem. Let

x \xrightarrow{F_1} x_1 \xrightarrow{F_2} x_2 \xrightarrow{} \cdots \xrightarrow{F_n} x_n

\mathsf{Env}(x_n)

\mathfrak{P}_I

\varepsilon_{k+1}\le \|F_{k+1}\|\varepsilon_k+\delta_{k+1},

(c,Q)\mapsto (Ac+b,\ AQA^\top + R),

This yields the Error Propagation Theorem.

Theorem I.3 (Typed Error Propagation Theorem). Let be a lawful operator with declared conditioning profile and let be a lawful envelope on . Then there exists a transported envelope

F_\#\mathsf{Env}_X

has a declared metric and form;

has a declared propagation law for that form;

the required conditioning data are present;

all assumptions needed for transport are explicitly declared.

Proof. The existence of a transported envelope requires a rule that takes carrier uncertainty on to carrier uncertainty on . Such a rule depends on the envelope form, the metric, and the conditioning of . Without those, there is no unique lawful pushforward. With them, the pushforward is defined by the appropriate branch of . Hence the conditions are both necessary and sufficient.

Conditioning now becomes central. Let be a map used to decode, invert, project, or lift a carrier. The conditioning profile of is

\mathsf{Cond}(F)=\big(\kappa(F),\sigma(F),\mathsf{Zone}(F),\mathsf{Risk}(F)\big),

is the condition number or analogous sensitivity scalar;

is the singularity distance or stability margin;

is the risk zone of the current operating point;

is the classified instability level.

The exact formulas depend on the domain, but the architectural role does not. Conditioning determines whether a small envelope on the input side remains small under transport or blows up into inadmissibility. Appendix I therefore states:

Law I.4 (Conditioning Visibility Law). No inverse, pseudo-inverse, deconvolution, lift, unfold, unmixing, or boundary reconstruction step may be treated as admissible unless its conditioning profile is either certified stable or explicitly ledgered as a risk factor.

This is the Cloud-lens counterpart to the no-hidden-loss laws elsewhere in the manuscript.

The appendix now introduces the entropy layer proper. Let denote the uncertainty or disorder load associated with a node, route, witness bundle, or manifested state . This entropy is not restricted to thermodynamic entropy in the narrow physical sense. In the manuscript it functions as a generalized uncertainty, instability, or control-deviation measure. The live corpus already states this clearly in related kernel notes and gives the appendicial role of entropy thresholds directly: if a node fails to reach the threshold after recursive cycles it is downgraded to ; cooling cycles tighten thresholds after high-intensity manifest operations; and a controlled chaos variable may be injected to test metastable resilience, with -bursts on the order of ten percent of the relevant regime threshold.

Appendix I therefore formalizes the Entropy Threshold Table as a map

\Gamma_I : \mathcal{R}\to \mathbb{R}_{>0},

the metastable band

  \Gamma_I(r)-\epsilon_r \le S(\eta)< \Gamma_I(r),

the failure band

  S(\eta)\ge \Gamma_I(r).

Thus a node is exact or operationally stable when it remains below threshold, metastable when it lies in the liminal band, and failed or blocked when it exceeds threshold. The threshold table is not one number for the whole manuscript. It is regime-specific and must be declared explicitly.

This gives the Entropy Admissibility Theorem.

Theorem I.5 (Entropy Admissibility Theorem). Let be a node in regime . Then:

if , the node is entropy-admissible for stable use subject to the remaining seating predicates;

if , the node is metastable and must not be silently promoted;

if , the node is inadmissible for -grade seating and must be downgraded, residualized, or quarantined according to context.

Proof. By construction of the threshold table, is the regime’s maximal admissible entropy load. The liminal buffer defines the metastable neighborhood just below that load. The three cases exhaust the order relation on . Their architectural consequences follow from the definitions of stable, metastable, and inadmissible operation.

The corpus’s explicit rule that a node failing to reach the threshold after recursive cycles is downgraded to must now be incorporated. Let be the current recursive-cycle count for node . Then the Recursion Degradation Law is:

n(\eta)\ge 4^4 \ \wedge\ S(\eta)\not<\Gamma_I(r)-\epsilon_r

\quad \Longrightarrow \quad

\mathrm{Truth}(\eta)\le \mathrm{AMBIG}.

The heat-sink invariant must likewise be formalized. The corpus states that every manifest operation must satisfy entropy neutrality: excess entropy must be redirected into the Quarantined Void or dissipated as computational heat in the CUT layer. Let a manifest operation have entropy change

\Delta S_M = S_{\mathrm{out}}-S_{\mathrm{in}}.

\Delta S_M + \Delta S_{\mathrm{sink}} = 0

Law I.6 (Heat-Sink Invariant). Every manifest operation that reduces local entropy or removes uncertainty from the active node must account for the displaced entropy through an explicit sink channel. No apparent increase in order may be treated as free.

This law prevents the ledger from faking purification by deletion. Entropy that disappears locally must appear in a sink, quarantine body, or dissipation ledger.

The cooling-cycle law is the next direct consequence. After high-intensity manifest or repair cycles, the corpus requires that the threshold be temporarily tightened to maintain local coordinate stability. This is formalized by a transient threshold update

\Gamma_I^{\mathrm{cool}}(r)=\Gamma_I(r)-\Delta_{\mathrm{cool}}(r),

\qquad \Delta_{\mathrm{cool}}(r)>0,

The -injection law is equally important. The corpus states that a node is not truly unless it can maintain coherence when exposed to a chaos burst equivalent to ten percent of its regime threshold. Let

\chi_r = 0.1\,\Gamma_I(r)

\mathsf{ResTest}_{\chi_r}(\eta)

\mathcal{C}(\mathsf{ResTest}_{\chi_r}(\eta)) \ge \Gamma_H(r),

Theorem I.7 (-Resilience Criterion). A node may be promoted to robust -status in regime only if it remains seating-admissible under the canonical -burst test.

This theorem is the first formal bridge between entropy thresholds and metastability recovery. Appendix J will later operationalize the recovery side; Appendix I fixes the test law itself.

The appendix must now define the ledger system that records all these events. The global error ledger attached to a carrier or process is

\mathcal{L}_I(\eta)=

\big(

\mathsf{EnvList},

\mathsf{PropTrace},

\mathsf{CondTrace},

\mathsf{EntropyTrace},

\mathsf{BudgetTrace},

\mathsf{AssumptionSet},

\mathsf{ReplayRefs}

\big).

is the set of current envelope objects attached to ;

records envelope propagation events across operators or route edges;

records conditioning changes and risk zones;

records threshold comparisons, cooling events, and sink routing;

records decisions based on finite resource envelopes;

records all assumptions for probabilistic or approximate claims;

records the pointers required to regenerate the ledger deterministically.

This ledger is mandatory. Error and entropy without a ledger are epistemically decorative and operationally unsafe.

The next crucial object is the budget family. Every search, route, witness expansion, or compile pass runs under finite budgets. The corpus already gives a canonical example: deterministic neighborhood expansion returns with a typed residual reason when vertex or edge budgets are exhausted, and routes to Appendix I as the budget policy anchor. Appendix I therefore formalizes a budget object

\mathsf{Bud}=(\mathsf{MaxVerts},\mathsf{MaxEdges},\mathsf{MaxOps},\mathsf{MaxBytes},\mathsf{Timeout},\mathsf{TruthFallback})

Law I.8 (Budget Exhaustion Law). If a process exhausts a declared budget before exact closure, it must emit a - or -class residual event whose reason is the budget family, not a generic “incomplete” label. Exhaustion is typed. It is never silent.

This law ensures that computational limits do not masquerade as epistemic uncertainty. A path may be unresolved because the graph is large, because the timeout hit, because the edge budget was exhausted, or because the assumptions are wrong. These are different ledger events.

The conditioning and singularity diagnostics now need a geometric form. Let be a local map with Jacobian or an abstract discrete analogue. The singularity risk zoning of a region is a classification

\mathsf{Zone}_F:\Omega \to \{\mathrm{safe},\mathrm{watch},\mathrm{critical},\mathrm{forbidden}\}

The probabilistic branch of Appendix I must likewise be exact. If an envelope is probabilistic, then the assumptions set must include:

the randomness source or ensemble source;

dependence or independence assumptions;

the estimator family;

the confidence construction;

the replay handle by which the same sample or a pinned surrogate sample is regenerated.

No probabilistic bound is lawful without this. In particular, bootstrap, Monte Carlo, and sampling-based uncertainty belong to and cannot be laundered into deterministic exactness. This follows directly from Law I.2.

The appendix also requires a drift-detection system. Drift is any divergence between expected envelope evolution and observed or replayed envelope evolution under fixed pins. Let

D_t = \mathsf{Env}^{\mathrm{obs}}_t - \mathsf{Env}^{\mathrm{pred}}_t

\mathsf{Drift}_I: D_t \mapsto \{\mathrm{normal},\mathrm{warning},\mathrm{critical},\mathrm{quarantine}\}.

The core theorem of the appendix is the Ledgered Honesty Theorem.

Theorem I.9 (Ledgered Honesty Theorem). Let be any manuscript object subject to approximation, truncation, routing thresholds, conditioning risk, probabilistic uncertainty, or finite budgets. Then is canonically admissible only if every such limitation is representable as a typed ledger event in , and all later truth, seating, and promotion decisions consume that ledger explicitly.

Proof. If a limitation cannot be represented as a typed ledger event, then later systems cannot distinguish exact law from bounded approximation or stable operation from metastability. In that case promotion, publication, or migration may silently outrun the actual uncertainty structure. Since the manuscript forbids silent loss and silent promotion, every such limitation must be ledgered. Conversely, if every limitation is ledgered and later systems consume that ledger, the process is honest relative to its corridor. Therefore ledger representability is both necessary and, in the architectural sense, sufficient for admissible honesty.

The local zero-point of Appendix I is the envelope-and-ledger kernel:

Z_I(\eta)=

\big(

\mathsf{MetricID},

\mathsf{Form},

\mathsf{Mode},

\mathsf{ThresholdClass},

\mathsf{BudgetClass},

\mathsf{EntropyClass},

\mathsf{LedgerDigest}

\big).

Integration with surrounding appendices is exact. Appendix D provides the proof templates whose constants and bounds are ledgered here. Appendix G provides convergence capsules and coherence cells whose residuals are classified in this appendix. Appendix H provides the manifestation ledger and coherence floors that consume the entropy thresholds and budget objects defined here. Appendix J uses the metastability band and -resilience laws of this appendix to drive recovery. Appendix K consumes the quarantine-routing outputs generated when entropy or drift cross their critical thresholds. Thus Appendix I is the cloud-side calculus that makes every later architectural decision numerically, probabilistically, and thermodynamically honest.

The compression principle of Appendix I is simple and absolute. The manuscript does not permit uncertainty to exist only in the author’s intuition. If an object is approximate, its approximation must be typed. If an object is conditioned badly, that risk must be exposed. If a route stopped because the budget ran out, that fact must be ledgered. If a node is close to coherence threshold but not above it, that fact must be named as metastability and not dressed as success. Appendix I is the appendix in which the manuscript refuses to hide uncertainty behind elegance. It is the exact body by which the system remains numerically and operationally truthful.

Appendix I

Appendix J — Recovery Architecture, Metastability Control, and Rehabilitation Semantics

Appendix J defines the recovery architecture of the manuscript: the exact object system, intervention operators, repair grammars, metastability controls, rehabilitation predicates, and replay-certified return paths by which a lawful crystal body that has drifted, overheated, fractured, stalled, or fallen into quarantine is brought back into admissible corridor alignment without falsifying lineage, erasing residual history, or silently upgrading truth. If Appendix I provides the global error calculus, entropy thresholds, and ledgered admissibility discipline that determine when a node or route is unstable, then Appendix J provides the exact architecture by which such instability is diagnosed, contained, cooled, repaired, retested, rehabilitated, and either reseated or permanently superseded. It is therefore the appendix of lawful return. Appendix J

The fundamental claim of Appendix J is that recovery is not an informal promise attached after failure. Recovery is a typed process with its own carriers, operators, budgets, ledgers, replay paths, and certification gates. A crystal object that exceeds an entropy threshold, fails a replay check, drifts beyond corridor bounds, accumulates unresolved conflict, or cannot complete within budget does not merely “try again.” It enters a governed recovery architecture. That architecture must be explicit because the manuscript forbids three things absolutely: silent continuation after failure, silent rehabilitation without proof-of-repair, and silent promotion from unstable to stable state. Recovery is therefore a first-class subsystem, not an afterthought.

Let be any lawful manuscript object—node, route, witness bundle, convergence capsule, compiler output, governance artifact, or publication bundle—whose current state has been judged non-stable or non-admissible by the relevant portions of Appendices G, H, and I. Appendix J attaches to a recovery object

\mathsf{Rec}(\eta)=

\big(

\eta,\,

\mathsf{Class},\,

\mathsf{Cause},\,

\mathsf{Plan},\,

\mathsf{Cooling},\,

\mathsf{Repair},\,

\mathsf{Resilience},\,

\mathsf{Rehab},\,

\mathsf{Replay},\,

\mathsf{Cert}

\big),

is the recovery class of the failure or drift;

is the typed cause bundle;

is the intervention plan;

is the entropy-reduction and stabilization phase;

is the structural or semantic correction phase;

is the post-repair stress and metastability retest phase;

is the rehabilitation decision body;

is the deterministic replay transcript proving the correction;

is the promotion-ready repair or rehabilitation certificate family.

This tuple is irreducible. A recovery without class is blind. A recovery without cause is non-diagnostic. A recovery without a plan is not recoverable but merely hopeful. A recovery without cooling cannot distinguish genuine repair from temporary overdrive. A recovery without resilience testing cannot distinguish repaired from fragile. A recovery without replay and certificate cannot lawfully re-enter the canonical body. Appendix J fixes this exact grammar.

The first task of the appendix is therefore classification. A destabilized object must be assigned to a precise recovery class. Let

\mathcal{R}_J=

\{

\mathrm{thermal},\,

\mathrm{budget},\,

\mathrm{coherence},\,

\mathrm{conditioning},\,

\mathrm{replay},\,

\mathrm{conflict},\,

\mathrm{branch},\,

\mathrm{governance},\,

\mathrm{transport},\,

\mathrm{publication}

\}.

This gives the first architectural law.

Law J.1 (Typed Recovery Classification Law). Every non-admissible or unstable object entering recovery must be assigned a unique primary recovery class and may be assigned a finite auxiliary class set. No repair or rehabilitation operator may be applied before classification is declared.

This law prevents generic healing rhetoric from replacing actual diagnosis. Different failure classes require different repair grammars, different cooling laws, and different certificates.

The second foundational object is the CauseBundle:

\mathsf{Cause}(\eta)=

\big(

\mathrm{RootCause},\,

\mathrm{TraceSet},\,

\mathrm{ThresholdsViolated},\,

\mathrm{DependencyBreaks},\,

\mathrm{ConflictSet},\,

\mathrm{AssumptionBreaks}

\big).

The first theorem of Appendix J is then immediate.

Theorem J.2 (Cause Sufficiency Theorem). A recovery process is architecturally admissible only if its CauseBundle is sufficient to reconstruct the entry into recovery under deterministic replay of the relevant trace and ledger state.

Proof. If the cause bundle cannot reconstruct the failure event, then repair is unguided and later replay cannot certify that the same failure has in fact been corrected rather than merely bypassed. Since Appendix J requires replay-certified return, the cause bundle must be sufficient to regenerate the destabilizing event. Therefore such sufficiency is necessary. It is also sufficient for admissibility at the diagnostic layer because no further hidden cause is permitted.

The next foundational object is the Recovery Plan:

\mathsf{Plan}=

\big(

\mathrm{PlanID},\,

\mathrm{TargetState},\,

\mathrm{OperatorStack},\,

\mathrm{Budget},\,

\mathrm{CoolingRegime},\,

\mathrm{ResilienceTests},\,

\mathrm{ReplayReq},\,

\mathrm{ApprovalReq}

\big).

The cooling phase is the first active recovery stage. Appendix I already defines cooling thresholds and the tightening law

\Gamma_I^{\mathrm{cool}}(r)=\Gamma_I(r)-\Delta_{\mathrm{cool}}(r),

\mathcal{K}_{\mathrm{cool}}: X \to X

S(\mathcal{K}_{\mathrm{cool}}(\eta)) \le S(\eta) - \Delta

This yields the Cooling Admissibility Theorem.

Theorem J.3 (Cooling Admissibility). Let be a recovering object in regime . A cooling phase is admissible if and only if it satisfies:

entropy reduction below the declared cooling threshold,

preservation of non-sacrificial invariants,

explicit sink routing for displaced entropy,

replayable cooling trace.

Proof. Entropy reduction alone is insufficient because illicit cooling could erase state unlawfully. Preservation of non-sacrificial invariants ensures identity is not replaced by amnesia. Sink routing enforces the heat-sink invariant of Appendix I. Replayable trace ensures that the same cooling process may be audited and regenerated. These conditions are therefore exactly the admissibility conditions for lawful cooling.

The repair phase is the structural core of Appendix J. A repair operator is not merely any transform that changes the object. It is a transform

R:X\to X'

invariant restoration: the relevant violated invariants are restored or brought within bounded residual;

lineage preservation: the repaired object remains linked to the pre-repair object by explicit migration or rehabilitation edges;

truth non-overclaim: the output truth class does not silently exceed what the post-repair witness and replay actually support.

This gives the Repair Operator Law.

Law J.4 (Repair Operator Law). A transform counts as a repair only if it restores violated invariants under explicit lineage and does not overclaim the truth class of the output.

This law blocks a common failure in self-repair systems: the object is replaced, relabeled, or simplified until the error disappears, but the resulting object is not actually the lawful descendant of the damaged one. Appendix J forbids such false healing.

A lawful repair phase therefore emits a RepairProof:

\mathsf{RepairProof}=

\big(

\mathrm{RepairID},\,

\mathrm{BeforeDigest},\,

\mathrm{AfterDigest},\,

\mathrm{InvariantDelta},\,

\mathrm{ResidualDelta},\,

\mathrm{LineageRef},\,

\mathrm{ReplayRef}

\big).

Recovery, however, is not complete after repair. The manuscript’s architecture demands post-repair resilience testing. Appendix I already provides the canonical -burst perturbation law:

\chi_r = 0.1\,\Gamma_I(r),

\mathsf{Resilience}=

\big(

\chi\text{-burst},\,

\text{cooling recheck},\,

\text{replay repetition},\,

\text{dependency rejoin},\,

\text{branch re-evaluation}

\big),

The resilience theorem is:

Theorem J.5 (Post-Repair Resilience Theorem). A repaired object is eligible for rehabilitation only if it passes the declared resilience suite, including the canonical -burst test for its regime.

Proof. A repair that restores nominal invariants but fails under standard perturbation remains metastable and cannot be treated as safely rehabilitated. Since the manuscript distinguishes stability from metastability sharply, post-repair resilience is required. The canonical -burst test is part of the regime law, so passing it is necessary for rehabilitation eligibility.

The next architectural object is the Rehabilitation Predicate:

\mathsf{Rehab}_J(\eta)=

\mathsf{CauseClosed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{CoolingClosed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{RepairClosed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{ResiliencePassed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{ReplayClosed}(\eta)

\wedge

\mathsf{ApprovalPresent}(\eta).

The rehabilitation theorem is therefore immediate.

Theorem J.6 (Rehabilitation Theorem). A recovering object may be promoted from recovery state to rehabilitated state if and only if .

Proof. The recovery architecture is defined so that each conjunct in closes one necessary dimension of lawful return: diagnosis, cooling, repair, resilience, replay, and governance. Omission of any conjunct leaves a gap in lawful return. Conversely, if all conjuncts hold, the object has passed every required gate. Thus the predicate is both necessary and sufficient.

The appendix must now define recovery states explicitly. A recovering object may inhabit one of the following states:

\mathrm{Diagnosed},\ 

\mathrm{Cooling},\ 

\mathrm{Repairing},\ 

\mathrm{Retesting},\ 

\mathrm{Residualized},\ 

\mathrm{Blocked},\ 

\mathrm{Rehabilitated},\ 

\mathrm{Superseded}.

if a lawful plan exists;

if cooling has reduced entropy below the cooling threshold;

if a RepairProof is emitted;

if the resilience suite passes and approvals are present;

if bounded residual remains but rehabilitation is not yet lawful;

if a contradiction or replay failure appears;

any stage if a lawful replacement route or migration body is declared and approved.

These states prevent recovery from becoming an untyped loop of “trying again.” They make return structured and replayable.

The manuscript must also distinguish rehabilitation from supersession. Rehabilitation preserves the identity lineage of the recovering object. Supersession declares that the object cannot be safely returned under its current lineage and must be replaced by a lawful descendant or alternative. This distinction is essential. Not every failed object should be rehabilitated. Some should be retired and superseded. Appendix J therefore requires a supersession criterion:

\mathsf{Sup}_J(\eta)=

\mathsf{Unrepairable}

\vee

\mathsf{BranchDead}

\vee

\mathsf{InvariantCostTooHigh}

\vee

\mathsf{GovernanceDeny}.

The appendicial relationship to quarantine must also be precise. Quarantine is not itself recovery; it is the containment shell in which recovery may be staged. Appendix J begins after quarantine has been entered or after a non-quarantine failure has been typed into recovery form. Its outputs are one of three things:

a RehabilitationProof path back to the canonical body;

a ResidualLedger path preserving bounded incompleteness;

a SupersessionBundle routing the lineage forward without pretending repair.

Thus Appendix J is not the appendix of containment. It is the appendix of lawful exit from containment or lawful abandonment of failed lineage.

The appendix must now state its implementation boundary. A recovery object must be realizable as:

class RecoveryRecord(TypedDict):

    object_id: str

    recovery_class: str

    cause_refs: list[str]

    plan_ref: str

    cooling_ref: str | None

    repair_ref: str | None

    resilience_refs: list[str]

    replay_ref: str | None

    approval_ref: str | None

    state: str

    truth: str

with validator output:

class RecoveryValidation(TypedDict):

    ok: bool

    rehabilitatable: bool

    supersede_required: bool

    residualizable: bool

    issues: list[str]

This code-level precision is required because the manuscript’s recovery claims are operational, not merely descriptive.

The local zero-point law of Appendix J is the recovery kernel:

Z_J(\eta)=

\big(

\mathsf{Class},\,

\mathsf{CauseDigest},\,

\mathsf{PlanDigest},\,

\mathsf{RepairDigest},\,

\mathsf{ResilienceClass},\,

\mathsf{Truth}

\big).

Integration with surrounding appendices is exact. Appendix I provides the entropy thresholds, cooling laws, -burst test, and drift diagnostics that trigger and shape recovery. Appendix H provides the manifestation ledger into which rehabilitated objects may be reseated. Appendix K receives those objects and routes them through the Quarantine / Execution / Boundary shell. Appendix L validates and replays the post-recovery transcripts. Appendix P maintains, migrates, and retires the resulting bodies over time. Thus Appendix J is the dynamic bridge between Cloud-lens diagnostics and executable return.

The compression principle of Appendix J is that failure does not abolish law. A destabilized object does not leave the manuscript’s exactness discipline; it enters one of its most demanding zones. Appendix J ensures that any return to admissibility is typed, witnessed, replayed, stress-tested, governance-checked, and lineage-preserving. It is therefore the appendix in which the manuscript proves that mercy and rigor are not opposites. Lawful recovery is mercy under exact form.

Appendix J

Appendix K — Quarantine Shell, Execution Boundaries, and Controlled Containment

Appendix K defines the quarantine shell of the manuscript: the exact containment architecture by which unstable, contradictory, over-threshold, unresolved, unapproved, or non-replayable objects are isolated from canonical execution while still remaining addressable, witness-bearing, replay-inspectable, and recoverable under lawful rehabilitation or supersession. If Appendix J establishes the recovery architecture by which a damaged or overheated object may be cooled, repaired, stress-tested, and returned, Appendix K defines the boundary regime in which that recovery can occur without contaminating the active crystal body. It is therefore the appendix of controlled containment. It specifies what a boundary is, when an object is routed into it, what can and cannot happen inside it, how execution differs inside and outside it, how conflict packets and quarantine records are formed, how proofs are preserved without promotion, and how lawful exit or lawful retirement is decided.

The governing claim of Appendix K is that quarantine is not deletion, and it is not mere refusal. Quarantine is a typed operational shell. A quarantined object remains part of the manuscript’s lawful universe, but only in a bounded mode. It may be replayed, diagnosed, cooled, repaired, residualized, branched, or superseded; it may not be silently seated, silently promoted, silently published, or silently used as an -grade dependency in the canonical body. The quarantine shell is therefore the exact boundary that preserves both rigor and recoverability. Without it, the manuscript would face a false choice between allowing unstable objects to contaminate the canonical body or erasing them and thereby destroying lineage and learnability. Appendix K resolves that false choice by making containment a first-class crystal object.

Let be any manuscript object: theorem, carrier, route, witness bundle, convergence capsule, governance artifact, migration body, publication bundle, or ecosystem rail packet. Appendix K attaches to a quarantine-shell object

\mathsf{QShell}(\eta)=

\big(

\eta,\,

\mathsf{BoundaryClass},\,

\mathsf{BoundaryCause},\,

\mathsf{ContainmentMode},\,

\mathsf{ExecutionProfile},\,

\mathsf{PacketBody},\,

\mathsf{RecordSet},\,

\mathsf{ReplaySet},\,

\mathsf{ExitLaw}

\big),

is the typed class of the boundary;

is the exact routing cause into the shell;

specifies the allowed behaviors within the shell;

specifies which operators remain executable and under what restrictions;

is the conflict or obstruction packet family by which the shell is addressed;

is the quarantine record family attached to the shell;

is the deterministic replay family permitted inside containment;

is the exact condition under which the object may be rehabilitated, residualized, superseded, or permanently revoked.

This object is irreducible. A shell without a boundary class cannot distinguish thermal quarantine from governance quarantine. A shell without a cause cannot justify its own existence. A shell without a containment mode is not operational. A shell without replay reduces containment to mere suppression. A shell without exit law becomes a prison rather than a recovery or retirement regime. Appendix K fixes all of these as exact required components.

The first task of the appendix is to define the universe of execution boundaries. Let

\mathcal{B}_K=

\{

\mathrm{entropy},\,

\mathrm{coherence},\,

\mathrm{replay},\,

\mathrm{governance},\,

\mathrm{conflict},\,

\mathrm{migration},\,

\mathrm{distribution},\,

\mathrm{trust},\,

\mathrm{budget},\,

\mathrm{publication}

\}.

The first governing law is therefore immediate.

Law K.1 (Typed Boundary Law). Every routed entry into quarantine must declare at least one boundary class in , and every subsequent containment or rehabilitation action must refer to that declared class. No object may enter quarantine under an untyped or generic failure label.

This law ensures that containment remains diagnostic and operator-specific. The manuscript does not quarantine because something “went wrong” in a vague sense. It quarantines because a named boundary was crossed.

The next foundational object is the BoundaryCause bundle:

\mathsf{BCause}(\eta)=

\big(

\mathrm{BoundaryClass},\,

\mathrm{ViolatedLawSet},\,

\mathrm{ThresholdTrace},\,

\mathrm{ConflictTrace},\,

\mathrm{ReplayTrace},\,

\mathrm{GovernanceTrace},\,

\mathrm{Digest}

\big).

The core theorem of boundary entry is then:

Theorem K.2 (Boundary Routing Theorem). A manuscript object is lawfully routed into the quarantine shell if and only if there exists a BoundaryCause bundle whose traces are sufficient to replay the boundary crossing event and whose violated laws forbid direct continuation into canonical execution.

Proof. If no sufficient BoundaryCause exists, then the shell has no exact justification and the object cannot be lawfully quarantined; it must instead remain in ordinary diagnostic or pending state. Conversely, if a sufficient BoundaryCause exists and the crossed laws explicitly forbid direct continuation—such as replay failure, exceeded entropy threshold, unresolved governance gate, or public export prohibition—then direct execution is inadmissible. In that case containment is the exact lawful response. Therefore the theorem holds.

The shell must now define its containment modes. A quarantined object is not simply frozen. It may be subject to one of the following modes:

\mathcal{M}_K=

\{

\mathrm{read\text{-}only},\,

\mathrm{diagnostic},\,

\mathrm{cooling},\,

\mathrm{repair},\,

\mathrm{replay\text{-}audit},\,

\mathrm{residual\text{-}holding},\,

\mathrm{supersession\text{-}staging},\,

\mathrm{distribution\text{-}block}

\}.

This yields the Containment Mode Law.

Law K.3 (Containment Mode Law). Every quarantined object must declare exactly one primary containment mode and may declare a finite auxiliary mode set. The operator family executable on that object is the intersection of the shell’s allowable operator set with the mode’s permitted operator set.

This law prevents covert execution inside the shell. One of the manuscript’s core prohibitions is that quarantine cannot be bypassed. Mode declaration is how that prohibition is operationalized.

The next foundational object is the ExecutionProfile. Let be the full operator family of the object’s native domain. Then the shell induces a restricted profile

\mathsf{Exec}_K(\eta)=

\big(

\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{allow}},\,

\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{deny}},\,

\mathcal{O}_{\mathrm{defer}},\,

\mathsf{Budget},\,

\mathsf{Pins},\,

\mathsf{AuditReq}

\big).

This profile leads to the Restricted Execution Theorem.

Theorem K.4 (Restricted Execution Theorem). Let be quarantined under execution profile . Then an operator may execute on if and only if:

;

the shell’s current containment mode permits ;

the required pins remain valid;

the containment budget is not exhausted;

the required replay/audit emissions are generated.

Proof. These five conditions are exactly the content of the execution profile and the containment mode law. Any omitted condition would allow an operator to act inside quarantine without the restrictions that define quarantine. Therefore they are necessary. Together they are sufficient because no further hidden execution constraint is allowed in a lawful shell.

This theorem is essential because it preserves a subtle but crucial point: quarantine is not inactivity. It is bounded activity.

The shell must now define its primary packet body. A quarantined object is addressed and transported through containment via ConflictPackets and ObstructionPackets. A packet is the minimal typed carrier that explains why the shell exists and what may be done inside it. The canonical packet schema is

\mathsf{Pkt}_K=

\big(

\mathrm{PktID},\,

\mathrm{ObjectID},\,

\mathrm{BoundaryClass},\,

\mathrm{Mode},\,

\mathrm{CauseRef},\,

\mathrm{AllowedOps},\,

\mathrm{BudgetRef},\,

\mathrm{WitnessRef},\,

\mathrm{ReplayRef},\,

\mathrm{Digest}

\big).

This gives the Packet Sufficiency Law.

Law K.5 (Packet Sufficiency Law). No execution, repair, residualization, or supersession action may be performed on a quarantined object unless there exists a current packet body whose digest matches the shell’s current boundary state.

This law ensures that shell actions are always tied to a current exact containment descriptor.

The shell must further define its record families. The RecordSet of a shell consists minimally of:

a QuarantineRecord, proving the object was lawfully routed into containment;

a ConflictRecord or ObstructionRecord, describing the specific boundary incident;

a ContainmentLedger, recording all shell-local events;

a ResolutionReceipt if any shell-local event closes one of the shell’s obligations;

a LiftRecord if the object exits containment;

a SupersessionRecord if the object is retired in favor of a lawful descendant.

These records give the shell persistent memory. Without them, quarantine would be operationally real but historically invisible, which the manuscript forbids.

The shell must also define its replay regime. A quarantined object is often replayable even when not admissible for canonical execution. Appendix K therefore distinguishes two replay modes:

internal replay, which replays the object within the shell for diagnosis, proof-of-failure, proof-of-repair, or bounded operator validation;

external replay, which would treat the object as canonically executable outside the shell.

Only internal replay is permitted during quarantine unless the object has already passed rehabilitation or supersession staging. This yields the Replay Boundary Law.

Law K.6 (Replay Boundary Law). A quarantined object may support internal replay but may not support external replay for -grade use until the shell exit law is satisfied.

This law blocks one of the most dangerous loopholes: replaying a quarantined object successfully in a shell-limited context and then treating that shell-limited success as if it were global admissibility.

The shell must now define its exit law. There are exactly four lawful exit families:

Rehabilitation exit, where the object remains itself under restored admissibility;

Residualization exit, where the object remains boundedly incomplete and is reseated only in a restricted truth class;

Supersession exit, where the object yields lineage to a lawful replacement;

Revocation exit, where the object is permanently excluded from canonical reuse.

Let the shell exit predicate be

\mathsf{Exit}_K(\eta)=

\mathsf{Rehab}_K(\eta)

\;\vee\;

\mathsf{Resid}_K(\eta)

\;\vee\;

\mathsf{Super}_K(\eta)

\;\vee\;

\mathsf{Revoke}_K(\eta).

The rehabilitation branch inherits from Appendix J but must be localized to the shell:

\mathsf{Rehab}_K(\eta)=

\mathsf{CauseClosed}

\wedge

\mathsf{CoolingClosed}

\wedge

\mathsf{RepairProofPresent}

\wedge

\mathsf{ResiliencePassed}

\wedge

\mathsf{ReplayClosed}

\wedge

\mathsf{LiftApprovalPresent}.

\mathsf{Resid}_K(\eta)=

\mathsf{ResidualBoundPresent}

\wedge

\mathsf{UpgradePathPresent}

\wedge

\mathsf{NoFalsePromotion}.

\mathsf{Super}_K(\eta)=

\mathsf{ReplacementExists}

\wedge

\mathsf{LineagePreserved}

\wedge

\mathsf{RetirementCertified}.

\mathsf{Revoke}_K(\eta)=

\mathsf{TrustFailure}

\vee

\mathsf{PersistentReplayFailure}

\vee

\mathsf{PolicyBan}

\vee

\mathsf{IrreparableConflict}.

This gives the Quarantine Exit Theorem.

Theorem K.7 (Quarantine Exit Theorem). A quarantined object may leave the shell if and only if exactly one branch of is satisfied and the corresponding exit record is emitted.

Proof. Exit without one of the four branches would be semantically undefined. Simultaneous satisfaction of incompatible branches would render the exit ambiguous unless a precedence law is declared. Appendix K resolves this by requiring a unique selected exit branch and an explicit exit record. This makes the theorem both necessary and sufficient.

The shell must also define precedence among exit branches. Rehabilitation takes precedence over residualization when full lawful return is available. Supersession takes precedence over residualization when a canonical replacement exists and bounded incompleteness would only burden the ledger. Revocation takes precedence over rehabilitation when trust or replay failure is structurally permanent. These precedence rules ensure deterministic exit selection.

The appendix now introduces the Boundary Shell State Machine:

\mathrm{Entered},\ 

\mathrm{Classified},\ 

\mathrm{Contained},\ 

\mathrm{Diagnosing},\ 

\mathrm{Cooling},\ 

\mathrm{Repairing},\ 

\mathrm{Retesting},\ 

\mathrm{Residualized},\ 

\mathrm{Lifted},\ 

\mathrm{Superseded},\ 

\mathrm{Revoked}.

when a BoundaryCause bundle is sealed;

when a packet body and record set are emitted;

if diagnostic mode is selected;

, , or according to plan;

when entropy is brought under the cooling threshold;

when a RepairProof is emitted;

, , , or according to the exit theorem.

This state machine is the exact dynamic backbone of the appendix. It prevents the shell from being a vague waiting room. It is an executable finite grammar.

The appendix must now define its implementation boundary. A quarantine shell must be realizable as:

class QuarantineShell(TypedDict):

    object_id: str

    boundary_class: str

    boundary_cause_ref: str

    containment_mode: str

    allowed_ops: list[str]

    denied_ops: list[str]

    packet_ref: str

    record_refs: list[str]

    replay_refs: list[str]

    state: str

    truth: str

with validator output:

class QuarantineValidation(TypedDict):

    ok: bool

    internally_replayable: bool

    externally_blocked: bool

    exit_options: list[str]

    issues: list[str]

This code-level exactness is necessary because the shell is not metaphorical infrastructure. It is intended to be executable in the manuscript runtime.

The local zero-point law of Appendix K is the shell kernel:

Z_K(\eta)=

\big(

\mathsf{BoundaryClass},\,

\mathsf{Mode},\,

\mathsf{PacketDigest},\,

\mathsf{RecordDigest},\,

\mathsf{ExitClass},\,

\mathsf{Truth}

\big).

Integration with surrounding appendices is exact. Appendix I supplies the threshold and drift events that often trigger shell entry. Appendix J supplies the repair and rehabilitation grammar executed inside or after containment. Appendix L will validate the replay traces and route them through proof-grade checking. Appendix M will provide the strong closure and finality bodies used by lifted objects. Appendix P will maintain, migrate, or retire shell histories over long timescales. Thus Appendix K is the executable boundary wall between instability and canonical body.

The compression principle of Appendix K is simple but severe. The manuscript does not permit a broken, unstable, or unauthorized object to linger in a half-accepted state. Nor does it permit the destruction of such an object merely because it is inconvenient. Appendix K solves this by making containment exact. It preserves the object, preserves its lineage, preserves its failure signatures, preserves its replayability, and preserves its possible futures—rehabilitation, residualization, supersession, or revocation—without allowing it to contaminate canonical execution. Appendix K is therefore the appendix in which the manuscript proves that a boundary can be both strict and merciful without becoming vague.

Appendix K

Appendix L — Validation and Replay Protocol, Typed Outcomes, and the AMBIG Calculus

Appendix L defines the manuscript’s validation body: the exact protocol by which operators, routes, subsystem integrations, closed cycles, convergence capsules, quarantine exits, and publication candidates are tested, replayed, certified, and assigned typed outcomes. Its role is structurally double. In one direction it is the Air × Dance validation shell of the crystal program infrastructure: the exact specification of what counts as successful reconstruction and replay, from unit tests through integration tests to full seed-to-seed round trips. In the other direction it is the deep semantic body of typed outcomes: the appendix in which the truth system is defined, ambiguity is treated as a lawful certificate rather than a defect, and nonselection, abstention, and branch ledgers become explicit objects rather than informal caveats. Appendix L therefore stands at the joint between proof and execution, between corridor law and replay law, between certification and abstention. It is the appendix that determines what the manuscript may truthfully say after it has actually tried to run.

The central thesis of Appendix L is that validation is not merely the checking of finished results against external expectations. Validation is a replay-structured semantics. A statement, operator, compiler pass, route body, or ecosystem bundle is valid only relative to a declared replay protocol, a declared evidence window, a declared corridor, and a declared outcome type. This means that validation in the manuscript is not Boolean by default. Some objects replay to exact identity, some replay to bounded residual, some replay only to a branch set, and some fail. The exact meaning of these cases must be typed, replayable, and non-coercive. Appendix L is the place where that regime is formalized.

The primitive truth carrier is the type

\mathsf{Outcome4}:=\{\mathrm{OK},\mathrm{NEAR},\mathrm{AMBIG},\mathrm{FAIL}\}.

Law L.1 (Truth-as-Type Law). Every validation verdict, replay verdict, route verdict, proof verdict, publication verdict, or abstention verdict must inhabit . No silent coercion, ad hoc severity scale, or narrative substitute may replace this type in truth-bearing contexts.

This law makes typed truth primary. It prevents the system from replacing exact outcome semantics with prose moods such as “mostly works,” “seems plausible,” or “not ready yet” when those phrases have not been reduced to one of the admissible outcome classes plus their supporting ledgers.

The semantics of the four outcome types are exact.

An object has outcome if and only if it satisfies all declared invariants, all mandatory tests, all replay obligations, all corridor conditions, all dependency closures, and all promotion guards required for its class. An object is not merely free of visible contradiction. It is replay-closed, witness-bearing, non-straddling relative to the declared corridor, and publication-eligible subject to governance. In practical terms, means that the object may be treated as canonically usable.

An object has outcome if and only if it is structurally lawful and operationally meaningful, but one or more declared limitations remain: bounded residual, incomplete but non-critical replay closure, budget exhaustion with actionability preserved, approximation within declared corridor, or an explicit upgrade path still open. is not a soft . It is a distinct truth class with explicit restrictions: it may support controlled use, recovery planning, or evidence-directed refinement, but it may not silently promote to .

An object has outcome if and only if the available evidence, under the declared corridor and replay window, certifies non-identifiability among two or more live alternatives. is not error. It is a positive typed certificate that the current system cannot lawfully select a unique branch without violating nonselection discipline. An outcome therefore obliges the system to preserve candidates, emit branch ledgers, and route the object into refinement or abstention protocols rather than forcing a false choice.

An object has outcome if and only if contradiction, replay break, corridor violation, quarantine condition, trust break, or explicit disallowance under the governing laws prevents lawful use, lawful refinement under current conditions, or lawful publication. is not merely “unsuccessful execution.” It is typed inadmissibility.

This semantics yields the first theorem.

Theorem L.2 (Exhaustive Outcome Partition). For every admissibly typed validation target , exactly one of is the lawful outcome relative to a fixed corridor, replay window, evidence set, and pin-set.

Proof. The corridor and replay regime determine whether closes exactly, closes with bounded residual, remains branch-nonidentifiable, or violates admissibility. These four conditions are exhaustive by design. They are pairwise incompatible when evidence, branch rules, and coercion laws are obeyed. Therefore every target receives exactly one lawful outcome.

The typed outcome system must now be made algebraic. The manuscript does not validate only isolated nodes. It validates compositions: operator chains, route stacks, theorem dependencies, convergence capsules, tunnel executions, governance transitions, and ecosystem distribution flows. Outcome must therefore propagate compositionally. Define a partial binary operation

\otimes:\mathsf{Outcome4}\times\mathsf{Outcome4}\to\mathsf{Outcome4}

is absorbing:

   \mathrm{FAIL}\otimes x = x\otimes \mathrm{FAIL} = \mathrm{FAIL}.

   \mathrm{AMBIG}\otimes \mathrm{OK} = \mathrm{AMBIG},

   \quad

   \mathrm{OK}\otimes \mathrm{AMBIG} = \mathrm{AMBIG},

composes to unless later stages either close its residuals exactly or expose hidden incompatibility.

only if composition preserves all shared invariants, does not create a new straddle, and remains replay-closed.

This is not simply a severity lattice. It is a typed algebra of admissibility under composition.

The corresponding theorem is:

Theorem L.3 (Typed Outcome Composition Theorem). Let and be validated under a fixed corridor. Then the serial composite inherits outcome according to the conservative algebra above, with exact promotion from or preservation under allowed only when residual or branch obligations are explicitly closed in the composite proof body.

Proof sketch. A failure in either stage invalidates the composition. An ambiguity in either stage remains unless branch discrimination or branch-preserving transport is explicitly certified. A near result remains near unless the downstream stage consumes its residual ledger. Exactness survives only under full invariant preservation and replay closure. The rules are therefore forced by the no-silent-promotion and no-silent-coercion laws.

The next foundational object is the AMBIG certificate. Because ambiguity is treated as an asset and not a defect, it requires its own exact object form. A lawful ambiguity certificate is

\mathsf{AmbigCert}=

\big(

\mathrm{Ctx},\,

\mathrm{CandSet},\,

\mathrm{AliasSet},\,

\mathrm{OrderingSet},\,

\mathrm{EvidenceWindow},\,

\mathrm{ReplayRef},\,

\mathrm{NonSelectionSeal},\,

\mathrm{RefinementPlan}

\big).

is the exact context digest under which ambiguity is certified;

is the live candidate set;

records representational or semantic aliasing classes;
